Part VI.— Milk Supply, Unclean and Tuberculous (see pages 141, 142). Milk and Dairies Bills, 1909 and 1910. Metropolitan Sewers and Drains Bill. Milk and Dairies Bill, 1909. A Bill to make better provision with respect to the Sale of Milk and the Regulation of Dairies. Presented by Mr. Burns, supported by Sir Edward Strachey, Mr. Attorney-General for Ireland and Mr. Masterman. Ordered by the House of Commons to be printed 25th May, 1909. Memorandum. The main objects of the Bill are to provide for— 1. The more effective registration of dairies and dairymen. 2. The inspection of dairies and the examination of cows therein. 3. The prohibition of the supply of milk from a dairy where such a supply has caused or would be likely to cause infectious diseases, including tuberculosis. 4. The prevention of the sale of tuberculous milk. 5. The regulation of the importation of milk so as to prevent danger to public health arising therefrom. 192 6. The issue of regulations for securing the supply of pure and wholesome milk. 7. The establishment by local authorities in populous places of milk depots for the sale of milk specially prepared for infants. The provisions as to registration supersede the provisions as to the registration of dairies contained in the Contagious Diseases (Animals) Acts and the Orders made thereunder. The provisions as to the inspection of dairies and the prohibition of the supply of milk reproduce with amendment Section 4 of the Infectious Diseases Prevention Act, 1890, Section 71 of the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, and the model milk clauses incorporated in many local Acts. The clause as to the prevention of the sale of tuberculous milk is also taken from the model milk clauses, but the scope of the enactment is somewhat extended. The Board of Agriculture and Fisheries will, in connection with this Bill, issue an order under the Diseases of Animals Act, 1894, dealing with the notification of tuberculosis in cattle and the inspection, examination, detention, isolation and slaughter of tuberculous cattle, and the giving of compensation in appropriate cases. This Bill was dropped and a new Bill has been promoted. Milk and Dairies Bill, 1910. A Bill to make better provision with respect to the Sale of Milk and the Regulation of Dairies. Ordered to be brought in by Mr. Courthope, Mr. Long, Mr. Hayes Fisher, Sir Luke White, Colonel Lockwood, Mr. Courtnay Warner, Mr. Eyland Adkins, Mr. Charles Bathurst, Mr. Dawes, Mr. Guinness, Captain Jessel and Mr. Stainer. Ordered by the House of Commons to be printed 13th April, 1910. Memorandum. The main objects of the Bill are to provide for- 1. The more effective registration of dairies and dainmen. 193 2. The inspection of dairies and the examination of cows therein. 3. The prohibition of the supply of milk from a dairy where such a supply has caused or would be likely to cause infectious disease, including tuberculosis. 4. The prevention of the sale of tuberculous milk. 5. The regulation of the importation of milk so as to prevent danger to public health arising therefrom. 6. The issue of regulations for securing the supply of pure and wholesome milk. The provisions as to registration supersede the provisions as to the registration of dairies contained in the Contagious Diseases (Animals) Acts and the Orders made thereunder. The provisions as to the inspection of dairies and the prohibition of the supply of milk reproduce with amendment Section 4 of the Infectious Diseases (Prevention) Act, 1890, Section 71 of the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, and the milk clauses incorporated in many local Acts. The clause as to the prevention of the sale of tuberculous milk is taken from the Public Health (Scotland) Act, 1897. The Board of Agriculture and Fisheries have prepared an order under the Diseases of Animals Act, 1894, dealing with the notification of tuberculosis in cattle, and the inspection, examination, detention, isolation and slaughter of tuberculous cattle and the giving of compensation in appropriate cases. (See page 151 as to proposed amendment of Sale of Food and Drugs Acts as to warranties in the case of milk.) Metropolitan Sewers and Drains Bill (see page 176). Memorandum. The object of this Bill is to amend the state of the law relating to combined drainage. There are two kinds of combined drain, the " combined drain,'' which in law is a "drain," and the "combined drain," which in law is a 194 "sewer." The former is repairable by the private owner; the latter by the public authority. In the opinion of builders, owners and local authorities combined drains were originally constructed as drains, and were mutually regarded as such until the retrospective case of Travis v. Uttley (1893), the effect of which has been to convert thousands of drains, which had been privately owned and privately maintained, into sewers vested in the local authorities and maintainable at the expense of the ratepayers. The state of the law has been described by the Lord Chief Justice, who said in a recent decision, " It seems to me, as I have before pointed out, to be essential that there should be some amendment of the law upon this subject. The state of the authorities is such that it appears to be impossible either to reconcile the various decisions or to deduce from them any logical rule." Several provincial authorities, notably West Ham, Croydon, Carlisle, Leyton, Wood Green, Sheffield, etc., have been successful in obtaining the powers which the Metropolitan local authorities ask for by this Bill. Metropolitan Seweus and Drains. [8 Edw. VII.J A Bill to amend the Metropolis Management Acts with respect to Sewers and Drains. Be it enacted by the King's Most Excellent Majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this present Parliament assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:— 1. In and for the purposes of the Metropolis Management Acts, 1855 to 1899, and the Public Health (London) Act, 1891, or any Act or Acts amending the same, the word "drainshall be deemed to include any sewer or drain, whether constructed before or after the passing of this Act, with which two or more houses, buildings or premises are, at the date of the passing of this Act, or may at any time thereafter be connected, or which is used or capable of being or intended to be used for the conveyance of the drainage of such houses, buildings or premises directly or indirectly to any sewer which has been approved as such by the Metropolitan Commissioners of Sewers, the Metropolitan Board of Works, 591 or the London County Council, but shall not include any sewer so approved as aforesaid. 2. This Act may be cited as the Metropolis Management Amendment Act, 1908, and shall be construed as one with the Metropolis Management Act, 1855, and the Acts amending the same. On the back of the Bill appear the following names:—Mr. Dickinson, Sir William Bull, Mr. Bowles, Sir William Collins, Mr. Crooks, Mr. Timothy Davies, Sir George Fardell, Mr. Claude Hay, Sir Henry Kimber, Ear Percy, Sir Albert Spicer and Mr, Waterlow. The Boroughs represented are St. Pancras, Hammersmith, Lambeth, Woolwich, Fulham, Paddington, Shoreditch, Wandsworth, Kensington, Hackney and Islington. Coborn Road, 36; from front of house to sewer ,, 24, 26, 28, 30, 32; entire, across premises. Monier Road, 107, 109, 111, 113, 115; throughout to sewer. ,, 161, 163, 165, 167, 169; entire, across premises. 202 Council Sewers. Reconstructions by Borough Council as sewers:— Blondin Street 2 to 12 (even numbers) main drain throughout to sewer. Legal Proceedings. The owner of No. 21, Maverton Road elected to seek the opinion of a magistrate whether the main drainage of the premises was a sewer or drain. At the hearing of the summons the defendant was fined 10s. with three guineas costs for failing to comply with the terms of the statutory notice served upon him by the Council, the magistrate holding the system was a drain repairable by the owner. Smoke Nuisances. No case of smoke nuisance occurred in the district arising from without the district. Where nuisances have occurred within the district intimation and notice have been served and the nuisance abated thereon. Two cases of smoke nuisance arising from steam highway locomotives passing through the district were dealt with by letters of caution to the owners. Canal Boats Acts and Regulations. Under the Canal Boats Acts and Regulations 26 boats have been examined. Of these 9 were registered and 17 non-registered. All the registered canal boats, with one exception, were found in fair condition and in compliance with the Acts and Regulations. No contravention of the Acts was discovered on any of the nonregistered barges. Demolitions and Additions. No dwelling houses have been demolished during the year, but 63 additional houses have been built— Wrexham Road, 32 Jebb Street, 12 Ridgdale Street, 19 203 Unsound Food. The following unsound foods were dealt with during the year.— January 23rd.—Two tons of damaged butter for soap making. January 22nd.—330 tins sorted from 161 cases of condensed milk. January 22nd.—Two tons of damaged butter converted to "grease" at oil refinery. March 2nd.—Half a barrel of herring. June 21st.—12 boxes of tomatoes. July 2nd.—Box of plaice. August 5th.—24 tubs of pulped raspberries. August 13th.—3 trunks of plaice dabs. September 20th.-—Box of codling. Each of these parcels of food was condemned and destroyed. Offensive Businesses. The fat melters in the district have completed the necessary alterations to their plant and premises as required by the new regulations governing offensive businesses which came into force on November 25th, 1907, and has resulted in a remarkable diminution of complaints up to the present. Verminous Booms. 36 verminous rooms have been cleansed under the provisions of the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1902. Workshops and Workplaces. The workshops and workplaces have been visited and found generally satisfactory, any nuisances existing upon the premises have been abated on the service of intimation. Homework. The outworkers, who are all boot and shoe operatives, have been visited twice during the year, and the premises of each examined for nuisances and sanitary defects. The workrooms were mostly found in a fair condition, and any defects in the premises were remedied by the owner or occupier on a notice being served. 204 Milkshops and Cowsheds, Food Preparation, etc. The milkshops and cowsheds have given no cause for complaint; the cowsheds were limewhited and cleansed twice during the year, in accordance with the provisions of the Dairy and Cowsheds orders, and the milk vessels and measures of the various milk vendors were satisfactory with one exception, necessitating a caution to the vendor for uncleanly measure. The places where foodstuffs are prepared have been periodically visited. Ice Cream Makers and Vendors. On visiting the ice cream makers and vendors during the season, the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1902 was apparently carefully complied with. An alien itinerant vendor without name and address upon barrow was cautioned and at once proceeded to affix the necessary particulars. The barrow had recently been redecorated and the name slip forgotten. Food and Drugs Acts. Under the Sale of Pood and Drugs Acts fifty-three varied samples have been purchased and submitted to the Public Analyst for analyses On analysis one only was found to be adulterated. A summons was issued against the vendor. Particulars of adulterated sample and result of proceedings are appended. Milk.—Deficient in fat to the extent of 20 per cent. Defendant fined 40s. and 23s. costs. Eight samples of butter were mixed with a foreign substance, i.e., boric acid (preservative), in varying small proportions, making in all nine defective samples. Public Health Offices, Bow Road, E., December 31s£, 1909. To the Medical Officer of Health. I beg to submit my fifth Annual Report of the sanitary work executed in the Bromley North Division for the year ended 1909. The sanitary work executed was as follows:— 1622 premises have been inspected. 1317 in response to complaint of ntiisances. 188 on account of notified infectious diseases. 117 house-to-house inspections. Wellington Road, 74, 76. Bow Road, 54. Swaton Road, 60, 38. Perring Street, 17, 19, 18. Priscilla Road, 41-49. Botolph Road, 5. Box Street, 18. Egleton Road, 33, 34-40. Red Schools. Stepney Workhouse. Hawgood Street, 12. Eastward Street, 15. St. Leonard Street, 19, 21. Imperial Street, 1. Stewarts Cottages, 6. Hancock Road, 4, 5. Blackthorn Street, 74. 209 Food and Drags Acts. Under your instructions 51 samples of food stuffs have been purchased and submitted to the Public Analyst. The undermentioned articles were bought, viz.:— Milk, 25; butter, 15; coffee, 1; cocoa, 4; margarine, 2; golden syrup, 1 ; saffron, 1; mustard, 1; Lard, 1. The result of the analyses of above samples showed that some of the articles were found to be adulterated. Result of Summonses under Food and Drugs Act. Name. Article. Complaint. Pined. Costs. Albert Lew. Alexander .. Milk .. Deficient in fat to the extent of 13 per cent. £10 44s. Isaac Benjamin Butter Containing 70 per cent of foreign fat. £15 £5 5s. Jane Thomas Milk .. Deficient in solids not fat, 58 per cent. Nil. 23s. Elizabeth Roberts Butter Containing 2 5 per cent. of excess water. 10s. 2 s. Factories, Workshops, Workplaces and Outworkers. During the year the premises upon the Register have been periodically inspected, and where necessary, for sanitary purposes, notices have been duly served upon the responsible persons, and the nuisances were abated thereon. Milk Shops. There are 49 milk shops in the district and these were inspected periodically. On a few occasions the shop keeper had to be cautioned about the cleanliness of the milk vessels and utensils. The shop keepers are all duly registered by name. Cowhouses and Dairies. There are three cowhouses in the district and these are thoroughly inspected at least four times a year, to see that the cleansing is carried out, which is done without any trouble. Frequent inspections are also paid to see that the hands of the milkers are clean during the operation ; 210 I find that in some of the sheds a pail of warm water is provided for this purpose. Slaughter Houses. There are four licensed slaughter houses in the district. These are periodically inspected, and are kept in a satisfactory condition. Only small animals are allowed to be killed in these registered premises. Ofttimes a visit is made while slaughtering is in progress. Eating Houses. These were inspected and found satisfactory. Included under this heading are seven fried fish shops, which are visited for the purpose of inspecting the class of fish used in the trade and sold to the public. Bake-Houses. There are 20 bake-houses in the district, and all are regularly inspected. The work of cleansing is carried out satisfactorily. Hairdressers' Shops. There are 15 of these shops upon the register and they are visited frequently. The utensils used in this business are kept clean. Ice Cream Shops. There are many of these shops throughout the district, but on a small scale; the owners only supply the ice cream during the summer months, and during that period frequent visits are made and the utensils inspected. The place where the ice cream is stored over night is particularly investigated. Markets and Stalls. Much attention has been paid to these with a view of preventing the sale of unsound food. Night inspections have also been made, and good results have been obtained. The class of meat sold, has, in my opinion, been sound and fit for human food. Unsound Food. During the year a varied assortment of food stuffs have been surrendered by the owners as being unfit for food. Certificates were 211 given where the articles were destroyed. Large quantities of unsound food, etc., coming into the Bromley North District for destruction are destroyed under my supervision. These goods are handed over to the various inspectors after they have been rejected by the firms to which they were consigned. Smoke Nuisances. Many smoke nuisances have been notified, but on the service of an intimation the nuisance has been abated. Offensive Matter. There is a great improvement in the manner in which offensive material is conveyed through the district. Only on two occasions were carriers cautioned, but the nuisances were very slight. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, H. J. LANGLEY, Cert. Sanitary Inspector Exam. Board (Lond.) and Inspector under the Sale of Food and Drugs Act, and Canal Boats Act, Bromley North Division. 212 Report of Inspector, Bromley Central Division. Public Health Department, December 31si, 1909. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to submit to you my twentieth Annual Report of the Sanitary Works executed for the remedying of defects and abatement of nuisances, which have existed in the Central Division of the Sub-District of Bromley under the Public Health and Housing Committee of the Council for the Metropolitan Borough of Poplar for the year ended 31st December, 1909. Inspection of District. I have inspected 1,539 premises, 999 in response to complaints of nuisances, and notices received under the London County Council Bylaws and the Public Health Tuberculosis Regulations, 1908, 162 on account of cases of infectious diseases notified, and 378 were house-tohouse visitations. Of the 1,539 premises so dealt with 548 were found to be in fair sanitary condition, whilst in the 991 premises (the remainder) defects and nuisances were found to exist, which necessitated the following works of sanitary repairs (see tabulated statement page 181). In the supervision of same 4,788 re-inspections were made. Public Health Tuberculosis Regulations, 1908. Of the pulmonary tuberculosis cases for which notices were received, the great majority of patients were removed to various institutions for treatment. Inspections were made of the premises, as above stated, the necessary precautions (disinfection, etc.) adopted, and where required the work of cleansing was readily carried out by the responsible person. Drains newly Constructed and Reconstructed on the old lines of Drainage. Total number of dwelling houses, business premises, etc., in division, 3,192. Description of Premises Demolished, etc. Brunswick Road, premises adjoining Nos. 240 and 242 2 Coventry Cross Place, Nos. 1, 2, 3, 4, 5 5 Coventry Cross, No. 2a 1 Devas Street, No. 4 (rebuilt, added to No. 2) 1 Insanitary Dwellings. By the demolition during the year of the five small houses which comprised Coventry Place, commonly known as "Black Beetle Alley," a small unhealthy area had ceased to exist. The houses (5) were old, decayed and worn out. Four were three-roomed, back-to-back, atticbuilt, and one had two rooms. This last house was in a ruinous state, having been closed by the owner in December, 1906, to prevent legal proceedings being instituted. The five houses were without means of through ventilation, and the sanitary arrangements consisted of a draw tap for the drinking water and two closets in a small enclosed courtyard. No. 2a Coventry Cross, adjoining the above houses, comprised two rooms and an attic, lean-to wash-house at rear and a water-closet in a small yard, and these premises, although thoroughly repaired in July, 1904, had for a long time since been unoccupied, unowned and neglected. This house was also demolished. Brunswick Road. In consequence of damage done by fire to workshops and dwelling house adjoining 240 and 242 and the dirty and dilapidated state the premises were in, the owner closed and demolished the workshops and dwelling house. 216 House to House Inspections. Bromley Cottages. Leven Road. Croucher Place. Thomas Street. Dunbar Cottages. Thomas Place. David Street. Sections of Streets. Abbott Road. Oban Street. Brunswick Road. Portree Street. Byron Street. Railway Street. Bromley Hall Road. St. Leonard's Road. Colin Street. St. Leonard's Avenue. Chadbourne Street. St. Leonard's Street. Devas Street. Teviot Street. Donald Street. Venue Street. Empson Street Wellington Street. Findhorn Street. Wilson Street. Joshua Street. Willis Street. Marner Street. Wyvis Street. Moness Street. Drains Tested. The drains of 359 premises were tested by means of the "rocket" smoke test. Seventy-four were proved defective, not gastight, whilst in 285 cases (the remainder) the result was negative. The water test has been applied to all new drainage work, and also where practicable to drains partially reconstructed or repaired. Sale of Food and Drugs Acts—Margarine Act. I have, as directed by you, procured 50 samples of food, etc., which were submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis; one (milk) only being found to be deficient in fat to such an extent (33 3 per cent.) that legal proceedings were instituted. The vendor was fined £5 and 23s. costs. In addition to the above, two samples, one milk and the other butter, were not up to the standards. The vendors were duly cautioned by the Public Health and Housing Committee. The milk was found to be deficient in solids not fat to the extent of at 217 least 3.5 per cent., which deficiency indicated the presence of at least 3 5 per cent. of added water, and the butter contained 1.3 per cent. of excessive water. Altogether 19 samples of butter were obtained; 4 were found to contain boric acid, three 0 5 per cent. and one 0.25 per cent. Public Schools. Oban Street Council Schools. Bromley Hall Road Council Schools. Hay Currie Council Schools. St. Leonard's Road Council Schools. Marner Street Council Schools. The above schools were inspected and found to be in a fair sanitary condition; the drinking water supplies were drawn direct from Metropolitan Water Board's mains. The storage tanks were furnished with covers and periodically cleansed; these tanks are only used for supplies to lavatories and closets, etc. Inspection of Bakehouses, etc. I have, as instructed, made the periodical inspections of these (13) premises (three not in use), and, where required, served Extracts of Factory and Workshop Act, 1891, "intimations " and statutory notices for the necessary work of cleansing and repairs, which were respectively complied with. Hairdressers' Shops. The whole of the hairdressers' shops in the division were inspected, attention being given to the cleanliness of the utensils used in the business as well as to the sanitary conditions of the premises. Where defects existed, "intimations" and statutory notices were served and nuisances abated. Public-House Urinals, etc. Attention has been given to the urinals to ascertain whether they were kept clean and furnished with the necessary fittings in compliance with the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904. Verminous Booms. During the course of year 11 rooms were cleansed; it was not 218 necessary to enforce the provisions of the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904. Eating Houses, Coffee Shops, Pork Butchers, Sausage Makers, Fried Fish Shops. Inspections were several times made of the whole of the abovedescribed business premises and all necessary works of cleansing and repairs carried out, in some cases without the service of "Intimations," etc. In no instance upon such visits was there cause for complaint so far as the condition of food was concerned. Cowsheds, Milk Sellers and Purveyors. The above (51) premises were frequently visited, the Public Health, etc., Office Registers corrected in the cases of those found non-registered through change of occupancy. The new proprietors were supplied with forms which were duly signed for the required alteration. Constant attention was given to the enforcement of regulations relating to cleanliness of utensils, more particularly in compliance with the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1908, relating to the sanitary conditions and surroundings under which milk was sold. Upon notice received for renewal of the licence of a cowshed at 27, Abbott Road, the premises were again inspected and found to be in a fair sanitary condition ; no opposition was made to the application of the owner to the London County Council. Examination of Food. I have on several occasions, upon applications made by different itinerant vendors and tradesmen, examined articles of food purchased by them at the markets, and when found " unsound, unwholesome and unfit for food," witnessed the same destroyed by the owners, certificates being given to that effect. In no case was there any article of food "exposed for sale, deposited for sale, or in preparation for sale " at the time of my visit to any premises in such condition as to justify seizure. Ice-Cream Makers and Vendors. All the premises where ice-creams were made were visited, with the object of detecting nuisances and infringements of the London County 219 Council General Powers Act, 1902. The barrows were found to be legibly marked with names and addresses, etc., of vendors; and the utensils and the premises were found to be clean and the ice-creams were wholesome. Factory and Workshops Inspections. Nuisances arising within the several factories, workshops, workplaces, etc., were dealt with. The whole of the ascertained above business premises were inspected and found, in the majority of cases, to be in fair sanitary condition. In the remainder the work of repairs, cleansing, etc., was carried out in compliance with " intimations," notices, etc. Smoke Nuisances. Smoke emitted so as to be a nuisance from chimneys other than those belonging to private dwelling-houses, viz., factories, workshops, workplaces, etc., was abated on the service of the usual documents. In no instance was it necessary to resort to legal proceedings. Canal Boats. I have inspected 41 barges, 10 non-registered and one registered sailing barge; I found the cabins fairly clean, and no infringement of the regulations. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, RICHARD E. MINERS, Cert. San. Inst. Sanitary Inspector and Inspector under the Sale of food and Drugs Acts and Canal Boats Act, Bromley Central Division. 220 Report of Inspector West Combined Division. Public Health Department. 31st December, 1908. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to lay before you my ninth Annual Report of the sanitary work and other duties carried out under the different Acts in connection therewith in the West Combined District during the past year, rendering as far as possible a detailed account of nuisances abated, inspections made, summonses applied for, etc. Inspection of Division. In investigating complaints and making inspections of all kinds 1272 houses or other premises have been visited, 249 of these visits being on account of notifications of infectious diseases. In addition to these, 94 cases of pulmonary tuberculosis, notified under the new regulations, have been visited and dealt with as required. This number shows a further decrease upon those of the previous year. Of the 249 cases 11 were notified from the Poplar and Stepney Sick Asylum, 2 from Langley House Receiving Home and 4 from the Poplar Union. House to House Inspections. These visits to the number of 95 were carried out in the undermentioned localities, a large number of the drains proving unsound on being tested:— Ellesmere Street. South East Row. Langton Street. Ricardo Street. Prospect Place. Vesey Street. Park Street. Upper North Street. Sabbarton Street. and at odd houses as occasion required. 221 Drain Reconstructions. The drains of some 93 premises were taken out and reconstructed, and where practicable, in order to comply with the bye-laws of the London County Council and Borough Council, were intercepted, ventilated and provided with means of access for clearing in times of stoppages, the whole work being thoroughly tested before being passed as sound:— Barchester Street, Nos. 48, 50, 52, 54. Bath Street, Nos. 31, 15. Castor Street, Nos. 1, 2, 3, 4, 5, 6, 7, 8 (Elm Cottages, Nos. 1, 2). Chrisp Street, No. 180 (Maypole Dairy). Chilcott Street, Nos. 25, 27. Carmen Street, Nos. 5, 7, 9, 11, 13, 15, 10, 12. Emmett Street, Nos. 21, 23. East India Road, Nos. 80, 187a, Palm Cottage. Gough Street, No. 56. High Street, Nos. 25, 38, 40, 130, 134, 60. Hill Place Street, Nos. 28, 30. Southill Street, Nos. 27, 29, 31, 33, 35, 37. Sussex Street, Nos. 29, 30, 31. Langton Street, Nos. 7, 8, 9, 3, 4, 5, 6, Wiseman's Stables. Pennyfields, Nos. 29, 31. Wade Street, No. 22. Woollett Street, Nos. 7, 8, 9, 10, 11. Upper North Street, Nos. 121, 123, 125, 127, 129, 131, 133, 135, 137, 139, 141, 143, 145. Vesey Street, Nos. 19, 21, 23. The drains of 55 premises were also examined and amended where necessary. Coffee and Eating Houses. These premises have been periodically inspected during the year, alterations in tenancy and new shops have been registered and the registers brought up to date. While inspecting these places, so far as possible attention has been paid to the food in preparation for cooking. The premises have been cleansed when found necessary. Q 222 Food Inspection at Wharf, etc. At Aberdeen Wharf, where food, skins, and potted meats are landed for transit, inspections have been made from time to time and everything found in good condition. This wharf has been visited in company with an Inspector of the Local Government Board on two or three occasions. The butchers' premises and stalls in Chrisp Street Market were inspected at night times, at week ends and at times on Sunday mornings. In each place where sausages and brawn are made special attention has been given. These places are registered and the businesses are conducted in a clean and careful manner, and the premises are regularly cleansed. Odd consignments of damaged wheat, rice and barley have been received into the district from the " docks " to be made up into poultry food. These consignments have been watched through the processes. The following foodstuffs have been surrendered and destroyed during the year:— 24 boxes of tomatoes, 2 boxes of plaice, 1 lump of beef, 3 barrels of herrings, 1 box of skate, and several lots of damaged fruit in small quantities. Factories and Workshops. These places have been visited periodically, and when necessary cleansing "notices" have been served and complied with. New workshops opened have been placed on the register and duly inspected. No case of overcrowding or infectious disease in any workshop has been found to exist, but some cases of infectious diseases notified as residing in the district, but engaged outside the district, have been dealt with by notifying the authorities in whose district they worked. Outworkers. The premises where male outworkers live have been visited at 223 intervals. Changes of address have been noted and registered, and where necessary "notices" for cleansing have been served and complied with. Bakehouses. The occupied bakehouses now number 24 and these have been regularly inspected during the year. The bi-annual cleansing has been carried out satisfactorily and the places kept in very good order. Dairies, Cowsheds, Milkshops and Slaughterhouses. These places are regularly visited during the year. All dippers and storage vessels have been closely inspected as to cleanliness and have, generally speaking, been kept in a very good condition, and some of the milkpans are now covered with "patent dust-proof covers." All changes of tenancy (which are frequent) have been dealt with and the registers brought up to date. The number of these on the register at present is as follows:— Milkshops 69 Cowshed 1 Slaughterhouse 1 Canal Boats Acts. Canal boats that are "registered" under the Acts are visited as opportunities offer. They have been found, as regards the living quarters, in a clean and bright condition, and properly ventilated. The "certificates" have been produced at times, when asked for, and examined and compared with the number of occupants, and no overcrowding has been found to exist. No cases of illness have been discovered on the boats. Smoke Nuisances. Complaints from the London County Council have been dealt with, also my own observations of shafts. No legal proceedings were necessary as all "notices" were quickly attended to. 224 Food and Drugs Acts, 1875 to 1907. During the year 52 samples of various kinds have been purchased for analysis, 6 of which proved to be so adulterated that legal proceedings were instituted as under, and also "letters of caution" were sent to other vendors by order of the Committee where advised that this would be sufficient. Milk.—Deficient in fat to extent of 6.6 per cent. Summons dismissed on production of warranty. (1st offence.) Milk.—Deficient in fat to extent of 36 6 per cent., purchased from itinerant vendor on Sunday morning. Two defendants. First defendant fined £2 4s.; second defendant fined £1 3s. Butter.—Containing 7 per cent, excess of moisture. Milk blended butter. Defendant fined £10 and 23s. costs. Milk.—Deficient in fat to extent of 39.6 per cent. Defendant fined £2 and 23s. costs. Milk.—Deficient in solids not fat to the extent of 2.3 per cent., indicating the presence of at least 2 3 per cent, of added water. Letter of caution sent to vendor by direction of Committee. Milk.—Deficient in solids not fat to the extent of 3.5 per cent., indicating the presence of at least 3.5 per cent. of added water. Letter of caution sent to vendor by direction of Committee. Public Health (London) Act, 1891. All cases of infectious diseases notified during the year have received attention with a view to tracing their origin if possible. A summons was taken out against the owner of a house in Kerbey Street for not complying with a "notice" from the Council to do certain necessary works under the above Act. The defendant ignored the summons and did not appear at Court. An abatement order of 21 days together with 27s. costs was obtained. A further summons was taken out, and defendant again failed to appear to answer for disobeying the Magistrate's Order. 225 Defendant was further fined, and not paying the fines distraint was made by the Court on "goods" to the full value of fines. The premises are now empty and the work is to be done before occupation. London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904. Under this Act about 15 rooms have been successfully freed from vermin. No legal proceedings were necessary to ensure this result. The public-house urinals, as far as possible, have been kept in a cleanly state. Ice-Cream Regulations. London County Council (General Poivers) Act, 1902. All premises where ice-cream is made have been inspected and attention given to all the utensils used. Generally speaking the places were found in a clean state and likewise the apparatus. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, JOSEPH JOHNSON, R.P.C., Cert. San. Insp. Exam. Board (London); Sanitary Inspector and Inspector under Sale of Food and Drugs and Canal Boats Acts West Combined Division. 226 Report of Inspector, East Combined Division. Public Health Department, December 31sf, 1909. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to submit to you my fourteenth Annual Report of the sanitary work carried out in my district (East Combined Division) during the twelve months ended 31st December, 1909. Inspection of Division. 1659 premises have been inspected, 1424 in response to complaints of nuisances, 144 on account of notifications of infectious diseases, and the remainder (174) being house-to-house visitations. Of the 1659 so dealt with 983 were found to be in a fair sanitary condition, whilst in the remainder (676 premises) nuisances were found to exist, which necessitated the following sanitary works being executed (see tabulated list, page 181). Verminous Booms. 14 verminous rooms have been cleansed under the provisions of the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904. Bakehouses. By your instructions I have made periodical inspections of the bakehouses (numbering seventeen) throughout the district. Three of the bakehouses are underground. The bi-annual cleansing in each case was carried out satisfactorily. 230 The conditions in some cases necessitated service of "Intimations" with respect to the removal of sweepings from under the troughs and the cleansing of the utensils, etc. Cowsheds and Slaughterhouses. Five notices were received for renewal of licences. The premises were duly inspected in respect of the necessary cleansing and limewashing, which was done in accordance with the provisions of the Dairy and Cowsheds Order, any defects found were remedied before the renewals of the licences were granted. The slaughterhouses have been frequently visited, and at times when killing was in progress, and everything found satisfactory. The number of these premises now on the register are—cowsheds, 2; slaughterhouses, 3. Food and Drugs Acts. Under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts 53 varied samples have been purchased and submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis. Three on analysis were found to be adulterated, 1 only sufficiently to require the vendor to be cautioned by the Public Health and Housing Committee, whilst in the cases of the remaining two summonses were issued against the vendors. Particulars of adulterated samples and results of proceedings are appended :— Milk.—Deficient in fat and solids not fat to the extent of 26.6 per cent, and 11.2 per cent. respectively, indicating at least the presence of 11.2 per cent of added water. In pursuance of the different orders of authorisation granted by the Public Health and Housing Committee, it was not found necessary to institute legal proceedings in any case for the abatement of nuisances and non-compliance with the London County Council's and Poplar Borough Council's own bye-laws, as the nuisances were satisfactorily abated previous to applying for summonses. Smoke Nuisances. During the year the shafts throughout the district have been under careful observation, and in only four instances nuisances were detected. In these cases intimations and statutory notices have been served, which has had the desired effect of abating the nuisances. No recurrence of the nuisances took place, and therefore there was no necessity to institute legal proceedings. Unsound Food, Shops and Stalls. The shops and stalls in the district have been frequently inspected in respect of unsound and unwholesome food, and during the past year there was no occasion to seize any article exposed for sale. During the year 3 bags of young cabbages, 2 boxes of haddocks and 1 box of hake were brought to the Public Health Offices to be examined, and were found to be unfit for human food. After the usual precautions being taken to prevent any of the above being used after condemnation, the usual certificates were given for the purpose of the purchasers having their money returned by the wholesale vendors. 232 Coffee Houses, Restaurants, Private Hotels, Sausage Makers, Fried Fish Shops, etc. Periodical inspection has been given to these premises during the past year; change of proprietorship, new premises opened and those closed have been duly reported and noted in the register. At each inspection particular attention was paid to the food under preparation, and in no instance was there cause for complaint; in some cases it was necessary to serve intimations and statutory notices respecting cleansing of the kitchens, etc. Hairdressers' Shops. The whole of the hairdressers' shops throughout the district have been inspected, the sanitary condition of the premises, cleanliness of the articles used in the business being carefully noted. In some few cases intimations were required to be served. Generally there is a marked improvement in these premises. Factory and Workshops Acts. The workshops, domestic workshops, workplaces and domestic workplaces in the district where male labour is employed have been inspected, the number engaged in each case being checked, particularly in respect to overcrowding; the terms of the Acts relating thereto have been met with in response to intimation and statutory notices when necessary, and in no instance was there occasion to take legal proceedings. Canal Boats. The inspection of canal boats was without any particular incident during the year. Ice Cream Manufacturers and Itinerant Vendors. All the premises where ice creams are made have been inspected with the view of detecting nuisances, also any infringement of the London County Council's (General Powers) Act, 1902, Part viii. Each itinerant vendor's barrow and utensils have been inspected. In each case the manufacturer's name was found to be legibly affixed thereto, the ice cream and utensils were found to be satisfactory, and there was no cause for action to be taken. 233 Cleansing of Cisterns (Bye-laic under Public Health (London) Act. Section 50). The cisterns of the undermentioned buildings have been inspected during the year, and duly reported upon. Where covers were found to be defective, they have since been amended, and made as far as practicable dustproof. Each cistern is so situated as to be free from pollution:— Adelaide Buildings 2, Baffins Buildings 2, Grosvenor Buildings 55, Hudson's Buildings 2, Melbourne Buildings 4, Montreal Buildings 4, Ontario Buildings 4, Ottawa Buildings 4, Prestage Buildings 6, Quebec Buildings 4, Council Buildings 5, St. Lawrence Cottages, Norfolk Street 14, Sydney Buildings 4, Toronto Buildings 2, Winnipeg Buildings 4. Public House Urinals. The public house urinals have been under regular observation during the past year, and the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1904, Section 22, strictly enforced. Milk Shops and Milk Sellers. I have by your instructions made periodical inspections of premises where milk is stored and sold throughout the district with the object of enforcing the regulations of the "Dairies, Cowsheds and Milkshops Order of 1885," as amended by the Dairies, Cowsheds and Milkshops Amending Order of 1886, and the London County Council (General Powers) Act, 1908, Section 5 (Milk Clauses), in respect to the sanitary condition of the premises, cleanliness of measures, counter pans, means of storage, and prevention of contamination, particularly in respect to other articles kept for sale in the same premises. Where counter pans were not properly covered instructions were given to have proper ones provided. Number of Milk Sellers 33 Number of Milk Sellers, change of ownership 2 Number of Milk Sellers discontinued selling milk 5 Number of Milk Sellers added to Register 1 Overcrowding. During the year fourteen cases of overcrowding were discovered; in each case the nuisance was abated after the service of an intimation followed by a statutory notice, without recourse to legal proceedings. 234 Outworkers. The premises where male outworkers live and work have been inspected, and notices to cleanse the premises have been served where required. Riverside Wharves where Food is Stored, etc. There is only one wharf in my district, viz., Concordia Wharf, Cold Harbour (Ramornie Meat Co.), where food (all tinned) is landed, some of which is warehoused for other firms; the other, which is all examined by the consignee is for sale for both home consumption and export. A large amount goes into the Mercantile Service, all of which is examined and labelled by the Board of Trade officials before being taken away. The following number of tinned foods (as set out below) on examination were found by the consignee to be blown or otherwise damaged and consequently condemned by the consignee as unfit for human food; the condemned food was set apart by the consignee in a building adjoining the premises for the purpose of being sent to a fat boiler to be rendered down for the fat, proper precautions being taken to prevent the condemned food being used for any other purpose. 189 61bs. beef, 325 21bs. beef, 15 1lb. beef, 711 61bs. mutton, 17 41bs. mutton, 439 21bs. mutton, 81 21bs. soup, 13 21bs. tongue, 166 1lb. tongue, 31 l½lbs. chicken, 381 lib. salmon, 4 1lb. sausage, 8 1lb. ham, chicken and tongue, 310 tins of fruit—making a total of 2,690 tins. The "Regulations under the Public Health (Regulations as to Food) Act, 1907," give more power to inspect food imported into this country, and will facilitate a more rigid examination, also supervision of the disposal of unsound food. Public Schools. I have, as specially instructed, inspected the Public Schools in my district, particularly in respect to the water supplies and sanitary conveniences. The water supply for drinking purposes at each school was found to be drawn from the rising main, and the storage cisterns 235 (which are used for supplying the sanitary conveniences only) are cleansed periodically. The sanitary conveniences and offices were found to be in a clean and satisfactory condition. I am, Sir, Your obedient Servant, JAMES BULLOCK, Sanitary Inspector, Inspector under the Sale of Food and Drugs Acts and Inspector of Canal Boats, East Combined Division. 236 Report of Inspector, South Division of Poplar. Hairdressing and Shaving Rooms. The hair cutting and shaving rooms (20 in all) were inspected and dealt with where necessary. Smoke Nuisances. The number of complaints with reference to black smoke issuing from the numerous factory chimney shafts in Millwall and Cubitt Town have been considerably less during the past year. The nuisances occurring were in most cases abated on the service of an intimation, and when necessary followed by a statutory notice. The smoke-preventing appliances attached to many of the furnaces, in conjunction with careful stoking as the result of previous proceedings, repeated visits, and cautions, no doubt contributed to this result. 239 Inspection of Schools. Riverside Wharves and Food Manufacturing and Preserving Factories. Damaged or Unsound Foodstuffs returned from Abroad.—In response to notices from the Port Sanitary Authority of unsound foodstuffs consigned from the docks to the above factory, I have inspected the following goods on delivery, with the results indicated below:— 16 cases of sardines, each containing 100 tins per case. 127 tins unsound and destroyed, remainder sound. 24 Canadian cheeses each 601b. in weight. Damaged externally, unsound portions removed and destroyed. 241 2 cases calves' feet jelly, 36 jars per case. All unsound and destroyed. 3 cases tinned butter, 100 tins per case. External damage only to appearance of tins. Butter contained in sound condition. Maconochie's Wharf and Food Manufacturing and Preserving Factory West Ferry Boad. The above premises were constantly visited during the year, Particular attention was paid to the various food stuffs in course of preparation, as well as to the cleanliness of the vessels and utensils in use and of the sanitary conditions generally of the different kitchens and preparing rooms. All unsound or tainted food stuffs, blown or suspicious tinned food, etc., sorted out by the firm, were destroyed in the furnaces by the firm on the premises, mostly in my presence. The total amount of food stuffs destroyed (in my presence after being sorted out by the firm) during the year at this factory which consisted of meat, poultry, fish, soups, fruit and vegetables was 1858 tins, all of which was contained in tins varying from ½lb. to 14lb. in weight. Frequent exportations from the above factories of consignments of hams or tinned meat to the Argentine or Philippines (where a certificate is required from the Sanitary Authority of the district whence the goods are despatched to accompany each consignment) had occurred. In every instance the factory was visited and the foodstuffs (meat) examined prior to tinning before the certificates were signed. The additional powers conferred by the Regulations under the Public Health Regulations as to Food Act, 1907, facilitates a more rigid inspection of food stuffs landed at the above-mentioned wharves, and a more effectual means of dealing with and disposing of unsound food as defined in that statute. No notice under these regulations was received during the past year from the Officer of Customs relating to foodstuff imported into this division. The shops and stalls in the main thoroughfares were regularly visited. Surprise visits were made frequently on Saturday nights and occasionally on Sunday mornings. Although several small articles were 242 destroyed as suspicious or tainted, in no instance was I justified in seizing any food stuff exposed for sale during these visits. Foodstuffs Surrendered from Itinerant Vendors, Stalls and Small Dealers Premises. During the year, at the request of the owners, the undermentioned articles of food were examined at the Public Health Offices in some instances and on the district in others, and were found unfit for human food and were destroyed by the owners:— 1 trunk fresh herrings. 1 trunk cod roes. 1 trunk whiting. Sale of Food and Drugs Acts. Fifty-seven samples of food and drugs were purchased and submitted to the Public Analyst for analysis. Of that number 8 (being butters) contained boric acid preservatives ranging from .2 to .5 per cent. Of the remaining samples taken 3 were certified to be so adulterated that summonses were issued against the respective vendors. "Cleansing of Verminous Rooms." The intimations under this Act again proved very useful, 75 of which were served during the year, and resulted in 104 rooms being freed from vermin. " Water Supply in Tenement Houses In the month of March, notices were served under this Act to provide a proper and sufficient water supply at some tenement houses in Bromley. After a short delay the work was carried out, and there is now a supply tap and sink on each storey, which, needless to say, are greatly appreciated by the tenants. Nuisances. Legal Proceedings. In the month of April the landlord of No. 69, Arcadia Street was summoned at Thames Police Court for not supplying information, in order that the house should be placed on the register. The defendant alleged that the house was let to one family, but it was proved to the magistrate that he was collecting rents from more than one family. Fined 40s. and 23s. costs. San. I. Cert. San. Insp. Exam. Board (Lond.) Sanitary Inspector and Inspector of Houses Let in Lodgings. 249 Report of Health Visitor. Public Health Offices, Bow Road, E. January 1st, 1910. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— I beg to present the second Annual Report of my work. Poplar Health Visiting Association. The Poplar Health Visiting Association, of which I am organising Secretary, continues to do good, steady work. The five "Centres" into which the Borough is divided for working purposes are now properly organised and in good working order, each "Centre" having its own Hon. Secretary, Committee and band of "Helpers,'' the Hon. Sec. and two Delegates from each forming the Executive Committee, which is the ruling body of the Association. Consultation Days for Mothers and Babies are established in each "Centre"; these are held once a month, and the mothers may bring their infants to be weighed, and obtain advice on feeding and general management from the doctor in attendance. A "Provident Maternity Club" has been started in one "Centre." If this is successful, and the necessary funds are forthcoming, similar clubs will be started in each Centre. Several helpers have had to resign during the year owing to illness, removal or other causes, the number remaining on the list at the end of the year 1909 being sixty, including four doctors, five secretaries, and fifty-one visitors. To these, and to all who have so heartily co operated in helping forward the good work commenced by the Association, I should like to take this opportunity of expressing my heartfelt thanks, and trust that the success which has attended their first efforts will be an incentive to them, not only to continue, but to try and increase their efforts. The Association is composed of the following:— President Mrs. Sidney Buxton. Vice-President Mrs. R. H. Green. Hon. Treasurer Rev. H. Mosley. 250 North Bromley Centre. Hon. Sec. Mrs. E. Sinker. Hon. Reliable information regarding feeding, etc., of the infants visited by the voluntary helpers is not available, and as I mentioned in my last report, it is impossible for me to visit the cases before handing them over, which would be the better way; however, the following facts regarding the infants visited by myself, may, I think, be taken as typical of the whole. Of the 671 visited, 12 had removed, 17 were dead, and 12 were still births. The remaining ones were fed, at the time of visit, as follows : — Breastfed 92.0 per cent. Mixed feeding 3.3 ,, Hand fed 4.7 ,, 100.0 Number of mothers who worked during pregnancy:— Home work 8.7 per cent. Factory, workshop, charing, etc. 8 4 ,, Families occupying— 1 room per family 9.6 per cent. 2 rooms ,, 21.1 ,, It is now possible to give statistics regarding infants born from March to December, 1908. 922 were kept under supervision as far as possible, but of these 231 removed and were not traced. This does not adequately convey the difficulties met with when working amongst people of migratory habits, as some of these changed their address no less than five times. The total number of changes were 388, equal to 42 per cent. of the whole number visited, changing their address once. Of the 691 remaining, 72 died, giving a mortality rate of 104.19 per thousand visited, which I venture to think may be looked upon as a satisfactory result of the year's work, especially when one takes into consideration the fact that the worst areas in the Borough are mapped out for visiting. Soc.; Central Midwives Board, etc. S 254 Enquiry as to Industrial Employment of Married Women and Infant Mortality, 1908-9. 90 Cases. Home Office Returns. 14th February, 1910. To the Medical Officer of Health. Sir,— Respecting the sheets issued for analysis of cases, for the purpose of the Home Office Inquiry, still-births and miscarriages are not visited, so that no information regarding such cases is available. The cases are taken from Bromley, Poplar, Old Ford and Victoria Park, so as to be representative cf the whole Borough. They are all "casual-labour" districts, very few of the men being in regular work. The average income given is what they would have if they worked, but as 17.8 per cent. have been in receipt of Parish Relief, and others have been working under the Distress Committee sometime during the year, it will be seen that the average, low as it is, is too high. The women who work at home are match and cardboard box makers, trouser, coat and vest finishers, shirt makers, etc. All consider five shillings a good week; out of that they have to provide glue, cottons, etc., and use their own tools. The factory workers are "cutters down," fillers, etc., in match factories, packers in sweet factories. The few working "elsewhere" have done anything from hawking to nursing their neighbours during confinement. With regard to Habits.—None of the parents in the cases under supervision were abstainers, but the amount of drinking, especially amongst the women, is not to be compared with those amongst whom I worked in Liverpool, still, it is a matter for regret that the idea of beer being necessary to a nursing mother should be so deeply rooted. Quite a large proportion of the mothers prepare a proper dinner for the family when they have the means, with others, milkless tea and bread form the chief articles of diet, except for the husband—"who must have a bit of something, Miss." General Cleanliness.—Here again I must judge by comparison, and the sanitary arrangements are so infinitely superior to those in the provincial towns in which I have worked, that it must of necessity affect the home; the difference, to be appreciated, must be seen. Care of Children.—In the main they are as well cared for as can be expected. In my opinion it is impossible for any woman to give the 255 attention necessary for the well-being of the little ones when they are born, or to bear healthy children, when she is continually either suckling or carrying (sometimes carrying on both functions together) in addition to acting as general charwoman and nursemaid, and, in some cases, as breadwinner also to the family. That we cannot have quantity and quality is a fact very forcibly impressed on our mind every day. I have taken "infectious diseases" in the grouping of "causes of death" to mean notifiable infectious diseases, not including measles. I was not able in my Annual Report to make any comparisons of the mortality between the infants of working and non-working mothers, but have taken the opportunity to do so now. The result was so startling that I have prepared another Table for the purpose of comparison, which shows that the result in the present case is largely accidental. Table I. Comparison of rates of mortality between infants of working and nonworking mothers in the cases under supervision for the purpose of the Home Office Inquiry. PUBLIC SWIMMING BATHS. * * "The Morning Post directs attention to the dangers arising from public swimming baths. Every spell of hot weather produces a concerted rush to the swimming baths. After these periodic incursions a large number of the pilgrims suffer from colds or from internal disturbances which they commonly refer to chills suffered during their aberrant enthusiasm for the bath. This cause is more likely to be infection from the micro-organisms of the swimming bath if, as often is the case, the water in it is not renewed frequently or if the number of people who use it is large. Cases both of nose and ear affections have been traced to this source, and sometimes, though this is rare, typhoid enters the pool and spreads therefrom. These dangers apply not merely to indoor swimming baths, but to some swimming pools or lakes. Filtration has been tried without very much effect, sterilisation by heat is out of the question because of the expense, but sterilisation by chemicals offers a fruitful method because it has even been applied successfully (at Barking, for example) to sewage effluents. The application to a swimming bath of the methods of purifying sewage has been recently tried with satisfactory results. Hypochlorite of lime* in quantities sufficient to give 1 part available chlorine to 2 millions of water was found to afford efficient sterilization.f The swimming pool * The Electrolytic Fluid manufactured at Poplar is practically a solution containing hypochlorite of magnesia, which has the advantage of being non-caustic non-acid and non-poisonous. Other hypochlorites belong to the caustic and alkali and alkaline-like earth groups of substances. A hypochlorite of magnesia belongs to the magnesia group, and for commercial purposes can only be made cheaply by the aid of electricity. † For the three baths of over 80,000 gallons the strength of the fluid is kept as near as possible at 2-5 grammes of chlorine per litre, and for the two baths at Poplar at 2 0 grammes of chlorine per litre. 30, 20 and 20 gallons of fluid are added to the first three baths, 20, 20 and 20 gallons to the large Poplar bath and 10, 10 and 10 gallons to the small bath. If these additions be worked out it will be found they are sufficient to give one part of available chlorine to 1,600,000, 1,800,000 and 2,800,000 of water. * * See page 85. when so treated remained practically sterile for four days during constant use. No odour or taste from the chemicals is noticeable. How often such treatment need be applied must vary with local conditions, but probably the application twice a week in the proportions named would ensure a practically sterile swimming bath or pool."—Reprint, Water and Water Engineering, page 147, June 15th, 1910. Extract. Water Sterilization.* " ...We believe that the process (hypochlorite treatment) is not only " likely to be useful as an emergency method, but that ultimately it will " be accepted in this country as one of the ordinary steps in water " purification, and just as we now drink water which has been treated " with coagulants and filters to make it clear, so shall we be equally ready " to adopt a simple and cheap process, whereby the bacterial purity of the " water can be insured also. If we are content to drink waters which " have been treated with large quantities of sulphate of iron, why should " we reject without reason an infinitely small quantity of chlorine."— Reprint, The Surveyor and Municipal and County Engineer, page 803, June 10th, 1910. * The Surveyor and Municipal and County Engineer, pages 819 to 821. " Eight Examples of Hypochlorite Sterilisation of Water : Minneapolis ; Montreal; Harrisburg, Pennsylvania; Quincy, Illinois; Hartford, Connecticut; New Jersey; Toronto."
